## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t, which is the fundamental problem of determining rate laws in chemical kinetics. The rate typically depends on powers of concentration, and time-dependence may arise from autocatalytic, photochemical, or externally driven processes.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate dependence)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (transition between zero and first order)
- Autocatalytic with decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse first-order reaction)
- Reversible second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 + c1 * A + c2 (polynomial rate law from reversible reactions)
- Cooperative kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (A**c1 + c2) (sigmoidal rate dependence)
- Time-dependent decay: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (rate with time-varying rate constant)
- Cubic autocatalysis: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 * (c1 - A) (cubic autocatalytic scheme)
- Parallel reactions: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first and second order pathways)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition at high concentration)
- Square root kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**0.5 (half-order reaction, e.g., surface-mediated)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure concentration power-law dependence (dA/dt ~ A^n) → integer or half-integer reaction order from elementary or surface reaction mechanisms
- Polynomial in A with alternating signs → reversible reactions or competing forward/backward steps
- Product of A and (constant - A) terms → autocatalytic or logistic-type kinetics where a product catalyzes its own formation
- Rational functions of A (numerator/denominator polynomials) → enzyme-like or quasi-steady-state approximation from multi-step mechanisms
- Explicit time dependence multiplied by concentration terms → time-varying external conditions (e.g., temperature ramp, light intensity change)
- Negative constant plus positive A-dependent term → reversible reaction approaching equilibrium with nonzero equilibrium concentration
- Fractional powers of A (e.g., A^0.5, A^1.5) → chain reaction mechanisms or surface-catalyzed reactions with dissociative adsorption
- Sum of multiple power-law terms in A → parallel reaction pathways consuming the same reactant simultaneously
